# LLVM Optimization Pass Pipeline Propagation

## Your Task

Trace how an LLVM optimization pass is registered in the pass pipeline and executed. Find all C++ source files in `llvm/llvm-project` that participate in the optimization pipeline lifecycle: 1. The file that defines the `PassBuilder` class and its method for building the default O2 optimization pipeline (look in `llvm/lib/Passes/`). 2. The file that defines the `PassManager` template class — the core pass execution engine (look in `llvm/include/llvm/IR/`). 3. The file that implements `PassBuilderPipelines` which assembles the default module/function simplification pipelines. 4. The file that registers all standard passes via `PassRegistry.def`. 5. For a concrete example, the file implementing `DeadStoreElimination` in `llvm/lib/Transforms/Scalar/`. Report the repo, file path, and key class or function name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `github.com/llvm/llvm-project` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `github.com/gcc-mirror/gcc` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

There\n11: /// is no \"pass\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\n18: /// single module provided.\n19: ///\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\n21: /// modules and functions.\n22: ///\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\n24: ///   a Function.\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\n26: ///\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\n28: /// polymorphism as outlined in the \"Value Semantics and Concept-based\n29: /// Polymorphism\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \"Inheritance Is The Base\n30: /// Class of Evil\") by Sean Parent:\n31: /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\n32: /// * http://www.yout

Then check\n12: // that there are no uses that may read the location of the original MemoryDef\n13: // in between both MemoryDefs. A bit more concretely:\n14: //\n15: // For all MemoryDefs StartDef:\n16: // 1. Get the next dominating clobbering MemoryDef (MaybeDeadAccess) by walking\n17: //    upwards.\n18: // 2. Check that there are no reads between MaybeDeadAccess and the StartDef by\n19: //    checking all uses starting at MaybeDeadAccess and walking until we see\n20: //    StartDef.\n21: // 3. For each found CurrentDef, check that:\n22: //   1. There are no barrier instructions between CurrentDef and StartDef (like\n23: //       throws or stores with ordering constraints).\n24: //   2. StartDef is executed whenever CurrentDef is executed.\n25: //   3. StartDef completely overwrites CurrentDef.\n26: // 4. Erase CurrentDef from the function and MemorySSA.\n27: //\n28: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n29: \n30: #include \"llvm/Transforms/Scalar/DeadStoreElimination.h\"\n31: #include \"llvm/ADT/APInt.h\"\n32: #include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n33: #include \"llvm/ADT/MapVector.h\"\n34: #in

Doing this could\n207:   /// reduce implementation complexity and avoid potential invalidation\n208:   /// issues that may happen with nested pass managers of the same type.\n209:   template <typename PassT>\n210:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\n211:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\n212:     for (auto &P : Pass.Passes)\n213:       Passes.push_back(std::move(P));\n214:   }\n215: \n216:   /// Returns if the pass manager contains any passes.\n217:   bool isEmpty() const { return Passes.empty(); }\n218: \n219:   static bool isRequired() { return true; }\n220: \n221: protected:\n222:   using PassConceptT =\n223:       detail::PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\n224: \n225:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes;\n226: };\n227: \n228: template <typename IRUnitT>\n229: void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace(raw_ostream &OS, const IRUnitT &IR);\n230: \n231: template <>\n232: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Module>(raw_ostream &OS,\n233:                                                    const Module &IR);\n234: \n235: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Module>;\n236: \n237: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over modules.\n238: using ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module>;\n239: \n240: template <>\n241: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Function>(raw_ostream &OS,\n242:                                                      const Function &IR);\n243: \n244: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Function>;\n245: \n246: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over functions.\n247: using FunctionPassManager = PassManager<Function>;\n248: \n249: /// A container for analyses that lazily runs them and caches their\n250: /// results.\n251: ",

The `run()` method (line 190-191) is the execution method that runs all contained passes sequentially over the provided IR unit, calling each pass's run method and managing analysis invalidation based on PreservedAnalyses returned by each pass.\\n\\n5. **DeadStoreElimination** (llvm/lib/Transforms/Scalar/DeadStoreElimination.cpp and header): As a concrete example of a pass in the pipeline, the DSEPass class (defined in llvm/include/llvm/Transforms/Scalar/DeadStoreElimination.h:28) implements the `run(Function &F, FunctionAnalysisManager &FAM)` method.
